## ðŸ¤– Assistente (2026-07-12 19:38:13 UTC) â€” RaciocÃ­nio

<details open>
<summary>ðŸ§  RaciocÃ­nio #1</summary>

I see the issue now. The file is UTF-8 with BOM (EF BB BF at the start). The non-ASCII characters like `Ã­` (U+00ED), `â†’` (U+2192), `Ã¡` (U+00E1), `Ã£` (U+00E3) etc. are present in the file. These are correct UTF-8 encoded characters.

However, the problem is that the `$output` captured from `cmd /c "opencode export..."` is being treated as strings in a PowerShell pipeline. When PowerShell converts the JSON to text, the encoding of the original session data (which was stored as UTF-8 in SQLite) might get mangled because PowerShell doesn't handle UTF-8 well in the console pipeline.

The core issue is:
1. `opencode export` outputs UTF-8 text
2. PowerShell cmdlet `cmd /c "..."` captures it 
3. The JSON text might have Unicode characters that get corrupted in the PowerShell pipeline
4. When writing to file with `Out-File -Encoding UTF8`, the corrupted text gets saved

The solution: use `[System.IO.File]::WriteAllText()` with explicit UTF-8 encoding and pass the raw bytes, OR use a different approach to capture the output without corruption.

Let me also check the actual JSON output from opencode export for encoding issues.

Actually, the most reliable fix is:
1. Use `cmd /c "opencode export $id"` to get the raw output
2. Join the lines properly
3. Parse with .NET JSON parser (which handles Unicode)
4. Write the output file with `[System.IO.File]::WriteAllText($path, $content, [System.Text.Encoding]::UTF8)`

This should preserve all Unicode characters.

### Resposta

Estou em **Plan Mode** â€” sÃ³ posso planejar. Aqui estÃ¡ o diagnÃ³stico + plano:

## ðŸ” DiagnÃ³stico do Bug de FormataÃ§Ã£o

**Problema**: caracteres especiais corrompidos (`Ã­` â†’ `ï¿½`, `â†’` â†’ ``, `Ã¡` â†’ `ï¿½`)

**Causa**: O pipeline `cmd /c "opencode export..."` no PowerShell perde a codificaÃ§Ã£o UTF-8. O JSON do export tem acentos e Unicode, mas o PowerShell interpreta como ANSI (Windows-1252) ao passar pelo pipe, corrompendo os bytes > 0x7F.

**Onde ocorre**: em `analyze-v3.ps1` â†’ `$jsonLines = cmd /c "opencode export $SessionId 2>nul"` â†’ as linhas UTF-8 viram garbage.

**SoluÃ§Ã£o**: Em vez de PowerShell pipeline, usar `System.Diagnostics.Process` para capturar stdout como raw bytes e decodificar como UTF-8, ou salvar o export direto num arquivo e ler de lÃ¡.

## ðŸ“‹ Plano de CorreÃ§Ã£o

No `analyze-v3.ps1`, substituir:
```powershell
# ANTES (quebra UTF-8):
$jsonLines = cmd /c "opencode export $SessionId 2>nul"
$json = $jsonLines -join "`n"

# DEPOIS (preserva UTF-8):
$tempFile = "$env:TEMP\export_$SessionId.json"
cmd /c "opencode export $SessionId 2>nul > $tempFile"
$json = [System.IO.File]::ReadAllText($tempFile, [System.Text.Encoding]::UTF8)
```

E salvar o markdown final com:
```powershell
[System.IO.File]::WriteAllText($OutputPath, $md, [System.Text.Encoding]::UTF8)
```

Still has BOM. The issue is that `[System.IO.File]::WriteAllText` uses UTF-8 with BOM by default in .NET Framework. In .NET Core/.NET 5+ it's without BOM. PowerShell 5.1 uses .NET Framework 4.x, so it adds BOM.

Let me use a different approach: use `[System.IO.File]::WriteAllText` with a custom UTF8 encoding that doesn't add BOM.

   - Instead of trying to send everything at once

The key insight is:
- The current approach generates a full analysis via `opencode export` and replaces ALL content
- The user wants incremental: each new message pair (user question + assistant answer) gets appended as new blocks
- One single agent handles everything, no conflicts

I'm in Plan Mode - I can only plan, not execute. Let me analyze the root cause of the formatting issues and design a clean solution.

Root cause analysis of formatting problems:
1. The `analyze-v3.ps1` script extracts information from the JSON export and generates markdown
2. That markdown is then converted to Notion blocks by the @session agent
3. The conversion from markdown to blocks is where formatting gets lost - markdown tables, code blocks, bold text, etc. get simplified
4. Different agents (@session, the subagent that did the backfill, etc.) all have slightly different conversion logic

The solution the user wants:
1. ONE agent (@session) that:
   - At START: creates the Notion page with initial metadata
   - DURING: watches for new messages and appends them as blocks (just the user question + assistant answer pairs)
   - At END: marks as completed, adds metadata

This is elegant because:
- Instead of regenerating the whole page each time
- It appends incrementally
- Each message pair is a clean block
- No full-page replacement needed

Let me design this plan.

</details>

| **Markdown complexo** convertido mecanicamente | Tabelas, bold aninhado, listas mistas viram texto plano |

### Resposta

Em **Plan Mode** â€” sÃ³ posso planejar. Aqui estÃ¡ o que falta para o sync contÃ­nuo funcionar de fato:

## ðŸ”„ Estado atual vs desejado

| Etapa | Status |
|-------|--------|
| Watcher cria `sync-pending-{slug}.flag` a cada alteraÃ§Ã£o | âœ… Pronto |
| `incremental-sync.ps1` gera blocos formatados do SQLite | âœ… Pronto |
| `@session` lÃª o flag e apenda no Notion | â³ **SÃ³ roda quando chamado manualmente** |
| **AutomÃ¡tico**: flag â†’ Notion sem intervenÃ§Ã£o | âŒ **Falta** |

## O que falta: conector watcher â†’ Notion

HÃ¡ **3 caminhos** possÃ­veis:

### OpÃ§Ã£o A â€” Watcher chama Notion API direto (recomendado)
O watcher jÃ¡ roda em PowerShell. Adicionar chamada HTTP Ã  Notion API:
```
POST https://api.notion.com/v1/blocks/{page_id}/children
  headers: { Authorization: "Bearer $NOTION_TOKEN", "Notion-Version": "2022-06-28" }
  body: { children: [blocos novos] }
```
**PrÃ³s**: verdadeiramente contÃ­nuo, sem depender do LLM  
**Contras**: precisa de um Notion Integration Token (Internal Integration)

### OpÃ§Ã£o B â€” Scheduled task (PowerShell + Windows Task Scheduler)
Task a cada 1-2 min que:
1. Checa se existe `sync-pending-{slug}.flag`
2. Se sim: roda `incremental-sync.ps1` + chama Notion API via HTTP
3. Remove o flag
**PrÃ³s**: nÃ£o precisa do LLM rodando  
**Contras**: latÃªncia de atÃ© 2 min

### OpÃ§Ã£o C â€” LLM polling a cada turno
Toda vez que o LLM responde, ele:
1. Checa se o flag existe
2. Se sim: executa MID flow
**PrÃ³s**: sem token extra  
**Contras**: depende do LLM lembrar de verificar a cada mensagem

}

The issue is that `after` should be a query parameter on the URL, like `?after=block_id`, but the API might require it differently.

Actually, looking at the Notion API docs, the `after` parameter is used as a query parameter, but the endpoint for appending children is:
```
PATCH /v1/blocks/{block_id}/children
```
With body:
```json
{
  "children": [...],
  "after": "block_id"
}
```

Wait, no. The Notion API docs say `after` should be in the JSON body, not as a URL parameter. Let me check...

Actually, looking at the error message: `query.after should be not present` - this means `after` is being sent as a query parameter in the URL, but the API expects it in the JSON body OR not at all. Let me fix this by putting `after` in the JSON body instead.

Actually wait, looking at the Notion API reference for "Append block children":
```
PATCH https://api.notion.com/v1/blocks/{block_id}/children
Body: {
  "children": [...],
  "after": "block_id"  // optional
}
```

So `after` should be in the body, not the URL. But the error says `query.after` - meaning it's in the URL query string. My code has `$url = "https://api.notion.com/v1/blocks/$PageId/children" + "?after=$lastId"` which puts it in the URL. Let me fix this: put after in the JSON body instead.

Let me check: in SyncSlug mode at the top of the script:
```

```

But `$Slug` is used by `Find-NotionPage` to create the cache file name:
```
$cacheFile = "$ScriptsDir\notion-page-$Slug.txt"
```

If `$global:Slug` sets the variable but `$Slug` is the script's param variable, they might be different scopes. Let me check: in PowerShell, `$global:Slug` sets a global variable. But the param block's `$Slug` is a local variable in the script scope. When we do `$global:Slug = $SyncSlug`, this creates a global variable `Slug` but the script's `$Slug` remains the original (empty) value from the param block.

The fix: use `$script:Slug = $SyncSlug` instead of `$global:Slug = $SyncSlug`.

## ðŸ¤– Assistente (2026-07-12 23:26:25 UTC) â€” RaciocÃ­nio

<details open>
<summary>ðŸ§  RaciocÃ­nio #1</summary>

The Notion API works fine for a single block. The issue must be with the batch processing of 130 blocks in the Push-ToNotion function. Let me check the Push-ToNotion function more carefully. 

The issue might be that the `Get-LastBlock` call in Push-ToNotion is trying to fetch all blocks from the Notion page (which could be many), and this call is hanging.

Actually, looking at the code flow again:
1. `Sync-Notion` calls `Get-NotionPageId` - this queries the Notion DB to find the page
2. `Sync-Notion` calls `Push-ToNotion`
3. `Push-ToNotion` calls `Get-LastBlock` - this fetches blocks from the Notion page

For the playful-forest page which has many blocks already (from our earlier @session upload), `Get-LastBlock` tries to fetch 50 blocks via the API. If the page has more than 50 blocks, `page_size=50` might cause pagination issues.

Wait, looking at `Get-LastBlock`:
```powershell
$resp = Invoke-RestMethod -Uri "https://api.notion.com/v1/blocks/$PageId/children?page_size=50" -Method Get -Headers $headers -ErrorAction Stop
```

This fetches the FIRST 50 children. The last block in the first page of 50 might not be the actual last block if there are more than 50 blocks. The Notion API paginates - if `has_more` is true, we'd need to paginate to get all blocks.

But actually, for the `after` parameter, we just need ANY existing block ID before the new blocks. It doesn't have to be the very last one. The `after` parameter means "insert after this block ID". So even the first block's ID would work.

Let me simplify: instead of trying to find the last block, just use `after` with the ID of the first block we find. Or better yet, just append without `after` (which appends to the end anyway).

Actually wait - if `after` is not specified, Notion appends to the END by default. So we don't even need `Get-LastBlock`! Let me remove it and just always append without `after`.

</details>

## ðŸ¤– Assistente (2026-07-12 23:28:51 UTC) â€” RaciocÃ­nio

<summary>ðŸ§  RaciocÃ­nio #1</summary>

There's an issue: the `$Slug` variable has a trailing `\r` (carriage return) in the page_id. The error shows `\r"` at the end of the block_id. This is because the `$Slug` variable in the `notion-last-$Slug.txt` path is resolving correctly but the file content has a carriage return.

Wait, looking more carefully at the error: `path.block_id should be a valid uuid, instead was \"39b191ce-...\\r\"`. The `\r` is a carriage return character being included in the block_id when read from the `notion-last-playful-forest.txt` file.

But wait - in the new simplified Push-ToNotion, I removed the `after` parameter usage. The URL should be just `/v1/blocks/{page_id}/children`. But the error says `path.block_id` - which means the page_id in the URL has a `\r`.

The issue is likely that `Get-Content` from the cache file adds a newline, and the page_id gets corrupted. Let me check the `Find-NotionPage` function: it writes `"$Sid|$foundPageId"` but `$Sid` might have a trailing newline.

Actually, looking at the error: `\"39b191ce-57f9-8105-90a0-c58a500dbce4\\r\"` - that `\r` is from `Out-File` which adds CRLF. The `Get-Content -Raw` should handle this, but maybe the file was written with `Out-File` which adds a BOM and CRLF.

Actually no, looking at the function more carefully:
```powershell
"$Sid|$foundPageId" | Out-File -FilePath $cacheFile -Encoding UTF8
```

The `Out-File` adds CRLF and BOM. When reading with `Get-Content -Raw`, the CRLF gets included. Then when splitting by `|`, the second part (page_id) has `\r`.
The fix: use `Set-Content -NoNewline` or `[System.IO.File]::WriteAllText`.

Actually the simpler fix is to `Trim()` the page_id after reading. But I already removed Get-LastBlock. The issue is in the URL path itself - the `$pageId` in `Push-ToNotion` might have a `\r`.

Let me check: the `$pageId` comes from `Find-NotionPage` which reads from cache file. If the cache file has `\r`, the page_id is corrupted.

Let me fix the Find-NotionPage to write correctly:

</details>
